Jamison Brereton

11 (837)
Agni
HavirdhƒÅna ƒÄ·πÖgi
9 verses: jagatƒ´ 1‚Äì6, tri·π£·π≠ubh 7‚Äì9
This hymn, which has some phraseological echoes of X.10 but lacks its mythologi cal content, falls into two metrical parts, which correspond to its thematic structure. The last three verses (7‚Äì9), in tri·π£·π≠ubh, are fairly straightforward, describing the benefits that accrue to a mortal who serves the ritual fire and calling on Agni to bring the divinities to the sacrifice and let it begin.
The first six verses, in jagatƒ´, are far more complex, and, when viewed as a piece, without the three tri·π£·π≠ubh verses at the end, turn out to have an omphalos struc ture: the middle pair of verses (3‚Äì4) are parallel in structure, have the phrase agn√≠·πÉ hoÃÅtƒÅram ‚ÄúAgni (as) Hotar‚Äù opening their final pƒÅdas, and together treat both the1384 X.11
initiation of the current sacrifice and the charter myths for the introduction of the two ritual substances, fire and soma (with concomitant juggling of verb tenses). In verse 3 the first sacrificer, Manu, is present at the kindling of the ritual fire; verse 4 sketches the famous tale of the falcon‚Äôs theft of soma from heaven.
The outer verse pairs, 1‚Äì2 and 5‚Äì6, treat these two substances and their deified counterparts, fire/Agni and soma/Soma, both simultaneously and in parallel, with the referent often left unclear. The final verse of this section (6) is especially busy, with both Agni and Soma actively performing their ritual tasks at the same time (and perhaps under the same descriptions; see esp. 6c). The tentative identifications in that verse are made on the basis of the use of the phraseology in other parts of the RÃ•gveda. For example, the exact phrase ‚Äúhe trembles with his thought‚Äù is used of Soma in IV.71.3, and the verb translated as ‚Äúhe displays his power‚Äù (tavi·π£y√°) in that same pƒÅda has Soma as its subject in its two other occurrences. However, it is very likely that the poet expected the audience to consider both possibilities for the referent in each case and to grasp thereby the underlying commonalities of the two ritual substances. The first section of the hymn is thus a simpler example of the conflation of Agni and Soma found in the fiendish hymn V.44.

Jamison Brereton

The next ten hymns (X.10‚Äì19) form a Yama cycle, though the subject matter found in the individual hymns is quite various. Yama, the son of Vivasvant, is king of the land of the dead because he was the first mortal to die. Yet he was apparently born immortal (see esp. I.83.5) and chose to become mortal, subject to death, ‚Äúfor the sake of the gods…and for the sake of offspring‚Äù (X.13.4). The opening hymn in the cycle, the dialogue of Yama and his twin sister Yamƒ´, on the fraught topic of embarking on incestuous sex in order to produce offspring, addresses Yama‚Äôs change of status and his choice, but in a deliberately oblique and misleading fashion, as Yama spurns the sexual advances of his sister, and at the end of their bitter argument there seems little likelihood of children. The last six hymns in this cycle (X.14‚Äì19) are collectively known as funeral hymns. The first, X.14, is devoted especially to Yama in his role as king of the realm of the dead, while the others, especially 15‚Äì18, concern various aspects of death and the treatment of the dead‚Äîfor example, the forefathers who preceded us to Yama‚Äôs realm in X.15, the cremation fire in X.16, the funeral itself in X.

The intermediate hymns, X.11‚Äì13, have less superficially clear connections to the Yama saga, but both X.12 (vss. 6‚Äì7) and X.13 (vss. 4‚Äì5) make important comments on Yama and on Yama‚Äôs choice.

There is also an underlying unifying theme, that of duality and twinned-ness: the absolute disjunction between and the ultimate complementarity and unity of the mortal and the immortal, life and death, men and gods, men and women, heaven and earth, sacred and profane. It is appropriate that the cycle should begin with the dialogue between the primal twins, Yama and Yamƒ´, whose very names mean ‚Äútwin‚Äù and who bridge the gap between mortal and immortal.

Wilson

English translation:

‚ÄúThe great, the unconquerable (Agni), the showerer, milks openly with a (great) milking the streams (ofprosperity) from heaven for the unwearying sacrificer; like Varu·πáa, he knows everything by his understanding;may he who is skilled in sacrifice observe the sacrificial seasona.‚Äù

Jamison Brereton

The bull [=Soma] has milked out his draughts of milk for the bull [=Indra] by the milking of heaven‚Äîhe the youthfully exuberant,
undeceivable (son) of Aditi.
He [=Agni] knows everything, as Varu·πáa does, through his insight. Let him who is worthy of the sacrifice perform sacrifice throughout the
sacrificial sequences.

Griffith

THE Bull hath yielded for the Bull the milk of heaven: the Son of Aditi can never be deceived.
According to his wisdom Varuna knoweth all: may he, the Holy, hallow times for sacrifice.

Wilson

English translation:

‚ÄúThe Gandharvƒ´ and the water-consecrated feminine nine oblation praise Agni; may he be favourable tothe thought of me, raising my voice in his praise; may Agni plural ce us in the midst of the sacrifice; the chief (of theworshipers), our elder brother, repeats his various laudations.‚Äù

Commentary by SƒÅya·πáa: ·πögveda-bhƒÅ·π£ya

Agni: aditi·∏• = akha·πá·∏çanƒ´yogni·∏•, the indivisibleAgni

Jamison Brereton

The Gandharvƒ´ is murmuring, and let (that) watery maiden protect my mind all around at the bellowing of the bellowing (bull) [=Soma].
Let Aditi set us down in the middle of what we desire. Our eldest brother [=Agni] will proclaim (it) first.

Griffith

Gandharvi spake: may she, the Lady of the flood, amid the river’s roaring leave my heart untouched.
May Aditi accomplish all that we desire, and may our eldest Brother tell us this as Chief.

Geldner

Grassmann

Es rauschte laut Gandharva und die Wasserfrau; sie sch√ºtze bei des Stieres Toben meinen Sinn; In des gew√ºnschten Mitte setz uns Aditi, und unser √§ltster Bruder k√ºnd’ es uns zuerst.

Wilson

English translation:

‚ÄúThe very auspicious, resounding, famous Dawn, ascends bringing the sun to man; when for thesacrifice after the worship they give birth to that Agni, the desirer, the invoker of the desiring (gods).‚Äù

Jamison Brereton

And even now Dawn, rich in cattle, rich in glory, accompanied by the Sun, has dawned for Manu,
when they [=priests] beget Agni as Hotar for the ritual distribution‚Äîhim being eager for it and following the will of those who are (also) eager.

Griffith

Yea, even this blessed Morning, rich in store of food, splendid, with heavenly lustre, hath shone out for man,
Since they, as was the wish of yearning Gods, brought forth that yearning Agni for the assembly as the Priest.

Geldner

Auch diese gl√ºckbringende, Vieh und Ehren einbringende Usas ist aufgeleuchtet, dem Menschen das Sonnenlicht bringend, wann sie den verlangenden Agni nach dem Sinn der verlangenden G√∂tter als Hotri f√ºr das Opfer erzeugen.

Grassmann

Auch diese sch√∂ne, nahrungsreiche, herrliche, die Uschas, ging dem Menschen auf mit Glanz begabt, Als nach der will’gen G√∂tter Wunsch den willigen, den Agni sie, den Priester zeugten zu dem Fest.

Elizarenkova

‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§æ‡§É - (‡§∏‡§æ-‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç-‡§â ‡§®‡•Å) ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§®‡•Å ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‚Äù [‡§®‡§ø‡§ò‡•¶‡•®‡•§‡•Ø] (‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ) ‡§≠‡§ú‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ, ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä ‚Äú‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ú‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‚Äù [‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡•¶‡•™‡•§‡•Ø] (‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡•Ä) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä ‚Äú‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å-‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‚Äù [‡§®‡§ø‡§ò‡•¶‡•®‡•§‡•≠] (‡§Ø‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä) ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡•Ä (‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä) ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä (‡§â‡§∑‡§æ‡§É-‡§Æ‡§®‡§µ‡•á-‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏) ‡§ï‡§Æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§≠‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§≠‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§ø, ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø, ‡§Æ‡§®‡§µ‡•á-‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•á ‚Äú‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡§µ‡§É‚Äù [‡§∂‡•¶‡•Æ‡•§‡•¨‡•§‡•©‡•§‡•ß‡•Æ] ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á ‡§µ‡§æ ‚Äú‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§É‚Äù [‡§∂‡•¶‡•¨‡•§‡•¨‡•§‡•ß‡•§‡•ß‡•Ø] (‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç-‡§à‡§Æ‡•ç) ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡§ø (‡§â‡§∂‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç-‡§â‡§∂‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç-‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç-‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å) ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ï‡•Ç‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® (‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø) ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‚Äú‡§§‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç‚Äù [‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•¶] ‚Äú‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§•‡§æ ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§®‡•á‡§®‚Äù [‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡•¶‡•©‡•§‡•ß‡•®] (‡§ú‡•Ä‡§ú‡§®‡§®‡•ç ) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡••‡•©‡••

English translation:

‚ÄúThe hawk sent (by Agni) to the sacrifice has brought the dripping copious all-seeing (Soma) libatio·πáWhen the Arya people choose the victorious Agni as the ministrant priest, then the sacred rite is celebrate·∏ç‚Äù

Dripping: drapsam = not too much and not too little

Jamison Brereton

And this drop here [=Soma], widespread and widely visible, has the bird, the falcon that was sent (for it), brought here to the rite,
when the ƒÄrya clans choose wondrous Agni as their Hotar. And so was his insight born.

Griffith

And the fleet Falcon brought for sacrifice from afar this flowing Drop most excellent and keen of sight,
Then when the Aryan tribes chose as Invoking Priest Agni the Wonder-Worker, and the hymn rose up.

Geldner

Damals brachte diesen reichlichen, hellsehenden Tropfen der ausgesandte Vogel, der Falke zum Opfer. Sooft die arischen St√§mme den Meister Agni zum Hotri w√§hlen, entstand auch das and√§chtige Lied.

Grassmann

Auch jenen starken Tropfen, welcher weithin blitzt, hat hergebracht der Adler, zu dem Fest entsandt, So oft die Arjer sich den Agni ausersehn, den herrlichen zum Priester; dann ward Lied erzeugt.

‡§π‡•á ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∏‡§§‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§Ö‡§∏‡§ø ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§∏‡§ø‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§§‡•É‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ó‡•å‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§π‡•á ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡§É ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•à‡§É ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•à‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•à‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É ‡§∂‡•ã‡§≠‡§®‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§É ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§â‡§ï‡•ç‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∂‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§π‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∏‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§≠‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§É ‡§∏‡§π ‡§â‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø ‡§â‡§™‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§∏‡§ø ‡•• ‡•• ‡•Ø ‡••

Wilson

English translation:

‚ÄúYou, Agni, are ever plural asing (to your worshippers), as pasture satisfies (the herds); bewell-worshipped with man’s sacrifices; if commending the praise of the wise, and partaking of the (sacrificial)food, you come with many (divinities of the rite).‚Äù

Jamison Brereton

You are always delightful, like pasture lands to a prosperous man, (when,) o Agni, you conduct good rites with the libations of Manu,
or when, having ritually labored and having gained for the inspired poet a prize worthy of hymns, you journey near with abundant (gifts).

Griffith

Still art thou kind to him who feeds thee as with grass, and, skilled in sacrifice, offers thee holy gifts.
When thou, having received the sage’s strengthening food with lauds, after long toil, cornest with many more.

Geldner

Immer bist du erfreulich wie die Weide f√ºr den Viehz√ºchter, der du, Agni, mit den Opfergaben des Menschen den Gottesdienst gut verrichtest, oder wenn du mit vielen Gaben kommst, nachdem du deinen Dienst versehen und des Redners preislichen Lohn gewonnen hast.

Grassmann

Erfreulich stets wie Wiesen f√ºr den Weidenden bist Agni du, sch√∂nopfernd mit des Menschen Trank, Wenn eifervoll des Priesters sch√∂ne Labung du empfangen hast und zu uns kommst mit grosser Schar.

Elizarenkova

(‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡§É-‡§Ö‡§∏‡§ø) ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ã‡§∑‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡§∂‡§µ‡•á ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•É‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∞‡•ã‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§Ø‡§§‡§É (‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É-‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡§É-‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§É) ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§É-‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡•à‡§É ‚Äú‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‚Äù [‡§®‡§ø‡§ò‡•¶‡•ß‡•§‡•ß‡•ß] ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§ú‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‚Äú‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡§É ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‚Äù [‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡•¶‡•Æ‡•§‡•´] ‡§∂‡•ã‡§≠‡§®‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§∏‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø (‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç-‡§â‡§ï‡•ç‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§∂‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É) ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§£‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡•É‡§£‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‚Äú‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É‚Äù [‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡•¶‡•ß‡•§‡•´] ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‚Äú‡§∂‡§∂‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É [‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡•¶‡•¨‡•§‡•Æ] ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç (‡§µ‡§æ‡§ú‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∏‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç) ‡§Ö‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‚Äú‡§Ö‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ú‡§É‚Äù [‡§ú‡•à‡•¶‡•®‡•§‡•ß‡•Ø‡•©] (‡§≠‡•Ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§É-‡§â‡§™‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø) ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§™‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•à ‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§∏‡§ø-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§∑‡§ø ‡••‡•´‡••

‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡•Ä‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡•§ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§É‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡•á‡§™‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡•à‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§¨‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§Æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É‡••

Wilson

English translation:

‚ÄúWake up the parents, as the Sun his splendour; (the worshipper) desires to offer worship to (thedeities) who are plural ased by it; with all his heart he wishes (to do so); he desires to repeat (your praise); thebearer (of the oblation) is anxious to effect the good work; the sacrifice longs for augmentation, the prudent(sacrificer) trembles in his thoughts.‚Äù

Commentary by SƒÅya·πáa: ·πögveda-bhƒÅ·π£ya

The parents: heaven and earth, the parents of all living creatures; as thesun his splendour: jƒÅra·∏• = the sun,bhagam bhajanƒ´yam jyoti·π£; the prudent trembles in his thoughts: asura·∏• =prƒÅ·πáavƒÅn, breathing; or, praj√±ƒÅvƒÅn, intelligent;

Vepate = trembles, fearing lest the ceremony be defective

Jamison Brereton

Rouse his [=Agni‚Äôs] two parents [=kindling sticks], (as) a lover (rouses) his ‚Äúpiece of luck‚Äù [=girl]. The gladdening one [=Soma] is seeking to attain (the cows?) and sends (speech) from his heart. The draft-horse [=Agni and/or Soma?] is speaking; the bounteous one [=Agni?] is performing his work well. The lord [=Soma?] displays his power; he trembles (in poetic inspiration) with his thought.

Griffith

Urge thou thy Parents, as a lover ’ to delight: the Lovely One desires and craves it from his heart.
The priest calls out, the sacrificer shows his skill, the Asura tries his strength, and with the hymn is stirred.

Geldner

Errege die beiden Eltern wie der Buhle die Liebe! Der Erw√ºnschte hat ein Begehr; er fordert von Herzen dazu auf. Der Wortf√ºhrer redet, der Freigebige verrichtet gutes Werk. Der Asura zeigt seine Kraft, durch die Dichtung wird er beredt.

Grassmann

Erreg’ die Aeltern und als Buhle Liebesgl√ºck, der holde opfert und erquickt von Herzen gern; Er singet fahrend, sch√∂ne Werke wirkt der Held; voll Kraft dringt vor der Gott, er wird durch Lied erregt.

‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§æ‡§É - (‡§≠‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç-‡§â‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ø) ‡§π‡•á ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§ï ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç ! ‡§á‡§∏ ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§â‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§§ ‡§ï‡§∞ (‡§ú‡§æ‡§∞‡§É ‡§Ü ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§æ) ‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø ‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ú‡§∞‡§£ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡•à‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•á‡§ú ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§ï‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•á ‡§≤‡•á‡§ï‡§∞ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï ‡§§‡§ï ‡§™‡§π‡•Å‡§Å‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à (‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§É-‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É-‡§á‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡§ø-‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø) ‡§Ø‡§π ‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Æ‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§π‡§∞‡§®‡•á ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§® ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡§æ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§π‡§¶‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•á ‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à (‡§µ‡§π‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§É) ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§µ‡§π‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Æ‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§µ‡§π‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ (‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø) ‡§§‡•Å‡§ù ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§®‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à (‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á) ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§£ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à (‡§Æ‡§ñ‡§É ‡§§‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á) ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à (‡§Æ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§É ‡§µ‡•á‡§™‡§§‡•á) ‡§§‡§¨ ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•á-‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§ ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•á ‡§Ö‡§®‡•É‡§§‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞ ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§£ ‡§ï‡§∞‡§®‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ú‡§® ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Å‡§™‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à-‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡••‡•¨‡••

‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§ø - ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É

‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§æ‡§É - ‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï ‡§Æ‡§®‡§µ‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§ï ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û ‡§î‡§∞ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß ‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à, ‡§â‡§∏‡§ï‡•á ‡§™‡§æ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•á ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ü ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à, ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§≠‡•Ä ‡§®‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü ‡§π‡•ã ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à ‡••‡•¨‡••

‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§ø - ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É

‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§æ‡§É - (‡§≠‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç-‡§â‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Ø) ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§ï ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç ! ‡§≠‡§ó‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§Æ‡•ç ‚Äú‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§≠‡§ó‡§É‚Äù [‡§∂‡•¶‡•¨‡•§‡•ß‡•§‡•ß‡•§‡•ß‡•Ø] ‡§ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§Ø-‡§∏‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å (‡§ú‡§æ‡§∞‡§É-‡§Ü ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§æ) ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§∞‡§É-‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É-‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•å ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ-‡§Ü‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø (‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§É-‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É-‡§á‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡§ø-‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø) ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø, ‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•á‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§ø (‡§µ‡§π‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§É) ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É-‡§Ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä, ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ (‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø) ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ø‡§§‡•á (‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á) ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∞‡§§‡§ø (‡§Æ‡§ñ‡§É-‡§§‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á) ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§∏‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‚Äú‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§Æ‡§ñ‡§É‚Äù [‡§§‡•à‡•¶‡•©‡•§‡•®‡•§‡•Æ‡•§‡•©] (‡§Æ‡§§‡•Ä-‡§Ö‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§É-‡§µ‡•á‡§™‡§§‡•á) ‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ-‡§Ü‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§É ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•É‡§§‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§É ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§ú‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‚Äú‡§Ö‡§®‡•É‡§§‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‚Äù [‡§ï‡§æ‡•¶‡•Ø‡•§‡•ß‡•ß] ‡§µ‡•á‡§™‡§§‡•á-‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•á-‡§™‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡••‡•¨‡••

Wilson

English translation:

‚ÄúAgni, son of strength, the mortal who obtains your favour is widely celebrated; possessing abundantfood, and being conveyed by horses, illustrious and vigorous he graces the days of his existence.‚Äù

Commentary by SƒÅya·πáa: ·πögveda-bhƒÅ·π£ya

Bh≈´·π£ati =bhavati

Jamison Brereton

Whatever mortal will attain your favor, o Agni, son of strength, he is famed beyond (all).
Acquiring refreshment for himself, being conveyed by his horses,
brilliant and formidable, he attends upon (you) through the days.

Griffith

Far-famed is he, the mortal man, O Agni, thou Son of Strength, who hath obtained thy favour.
He, gathering power, borne onward by his horses, makes his days lovely in his might and splendour.

Geldner

Der Sterbliche, der deine Gunst erlangen wird, Agni, Sohn der Kraft, der wird √ºber die Ma√üen bekannt. Er bekommt gute Speise, f√§hrt mit Rossen; glanzvoll, m√§chtig sieht er den kommenden Tagen entgegen.

Grassmann

Der Mensch, der, Agni, deine Huld erlangt hat, der wird sehr weit ber√ºhmt, o Sohn der St√§rke; Viel Gut empfangend und mit Rossen fahrend schm√ºckt gl√§nzend er und kr√§ftig seine Tage.

‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§æ‡§É - (‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡§É ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§®‡•ã-‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á) ‡§ì‡§ú‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¨‡§≤‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§ï ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç ! ‡§π‡•á ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§è‡§∑‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•É‡§ï‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§π‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§Ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É‡•§ ‡§π‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡§µ‡§É ‡§π‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ß‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§§‡•É‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•É‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ú‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ú‡§∏‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§®‡§É ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§®‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§ß‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å‡•§ ‚Äò‡§§‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡§ô‡•ç‡§ô‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç (‡§™‡§æ. ‡§∏‡•Ç. ‡•≠. ‡•ß. ‡•©‡•´) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§π‡•á‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡§ô‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§§‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§ó‡§Æ‡§Ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡••

Wilson

English translation:

‚ÄúWhen, adorable Agni, this united praise is resplendent among the adorable gods, and when you,bearer of the oblatio, apportion the precious (treasures), then allot to us a valuable share. bring to us the heaven and earth, the daughters of the divine (PrajƒÅpati), let none of the gods be absent, and doyou yourself be present.‚Äù

Commentary by SƒÅya·πáa: ·πögveda-bhƒÅ·π£ya

The daughters of the divine: devaputre = devasya prajƒÅpater duhitƒÅrau; or, they whohave the gods for progeny

Jamison Brereton

When, o Agni, this assembly will become godly among the gods, a sacrificial one, o sacrificial one,
and when you will share out treasures, o you of independent will, then pursue a share for us rich in goods.

Griffith

When, Holy Agni, the divine assembly, the sacred synod mid the Gods, is gathered,
And when thou, Godlike One, dealest forth treasures, vouchsafe us, too, our portion of the riches.

Geldner

Wenn, o Agni, diese g√∂ttliche Versammlung unter den G√∂ttern stattfinden wird, die verehrungsw√ºrdige, o Verehrungsw√ºrdiger, und wenn du die Belohnungen verteilen wirst, du Selbstherrlicher, so sollst du da f√ºr uns einen g√ºterreichen Anteil ausbitten.

Grassmann

Wenn sich vollzieht die g√∂ttliche Versammlung bei G√∂ttern, Agni, heiliger, die heil’ge, Und wenn die Sch√§tze, herrlicher, du austheilst, so schenke hier uns g√ºterreichen Antheil.

Jamison Brereton

Hear us, Agni, in your seat, in your abode. Yoke the speeding chariot of the immortal one.
Convey here to us the two world-halves, whose sons are the gods. Don‚Äôt be the absent one among the gods; you should be here!

Griffith

Hear us, O Agni, in your common dwelling: harness thy rapid car of Amrta.
Bring Heaven and Earth, the Deities’ Parents, hither: stay with us here, nor from the Gods be distant.
